<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Athletics at the 2004 Summer Olympics</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

</table>
<p>At the <b><a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004 Summer Olympics</a></b>, the <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a></b> events were held at the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Athens)" title="Olympic Stadium (Athens)">Athens Olympic Stadium</a> from August 18 to August 29, except for the <a href="/wiki/Marathon" title="Marathon">marathons</a> (run from <a href="/wiki/Marathon,_Greece" title="Marathon, Greece">Marathonas</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panathinaiko_Stadium" title="Panathinaiko Stadium">Kallimarmaro Stadium</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Racewalking" title="Racewalking">race walks</a> (on the streets of <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Shot_put" title="Shot put">shot put</a> (held at the <a href="/wiki/Stadium_at_Olympia" title="Stadium at Olympia">Ancient Olympia Stadium</a>). A total of 46 events were contested, of which 24 by male and 22 by female athletes.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Participating_nations">Participating nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athletics_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Participating nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A total of 197 nations participated in the different Athletics events at the <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004 Summer Olympics</a>. Numbers in parenthesis indicate the number of athletes representing each nation.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athletics_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_aa"><a href="#ref_aa"><b><sup>a</sup></b></a></span> After the announcement of the disqualification for doping of the athlete <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yuri_Bilonog" title="Yuri Bilonog">Yuri Bilonog</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ukraine_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Ukraine at the 2004 Summer Olympics">UKR</a>), who won the gold medal at the time, there was a new distribution of medals in March 2013. According to a statement from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IOC" title="IOC">IOC</a>, the new owner of the gold medal went to <a href="/wiki/Adam_Nelson" title="Adam Nelson">Adam Nelson</a> (<a href="/wiki/United_States_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="United States at the 2004 Summer Olympics">USA</a>), the silver medal went to <a href="/wiki/Joachim_Olsen" title="Joachim Olsen">Joachim Olsen</a> (<a href="/wiki/Denmark_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Denmark at the 2004 Summer Olympics">DEN</a>), and the bronze medal went to <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Mart%C3%ADnez_Guti%C3%A9rrez" title="Manuel Martínez Gutiérrez">Manuel Martínez</a> (<a href="/wiki/Spain_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Spain at the 2004 Summer Olympics">ESP</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dsq1_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-dsq1-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dsq2_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-dsq2-2">[2]</a></sup><br/>
<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_bb"><a href="#ref_bb"><b><sup>b</sup></b></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Tsikhan" title="Ivan Tsikhan">Ivan Tsikhan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Belarus_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Belarus at the 2004 Summer Olympics">BLR</a>), was disqualified due to doping. There was no decision of the IOC to redistribute the medals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dsq1_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-dsq1-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dsq3_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-dsq3-3">[3]</a></sup><br/>
<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_cc"><a href="#ref_cc"><b><sup>c</sup></b></a></span> The United States victory has been in doubt since 2010 when <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Cox" title="Crystal Cox">Crystal Cox</a> (<a href="/wiki/United_States_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="United States at the 2004 Summer Olympics">USA</a>), who ran in the preliminary round, admitted to using anabolic steroids from 2001 to 2004. In July 2012, IOC decided to revoke the gold medal from Crystal Cox and asked the IAAF to make its decision about the US squad. On 31 May 2013 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IOC" title="IOC">IOC</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IAAF" title="IAAF">IAAF</a> announced that the result would stand, allowing the rest of the US squad to retain their medals and that they considered the case closed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><br/>
<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_dd"><a href="#ref_dd"><b><sup>d</sup></b></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Svetlana_Krivelyova" title="Svetlana Krivelyova">Svetlana Krivelyova</a> (<a href="/wiki/Russia_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Russia at the 2004 Summer Olympics">RUS</a>), was disqualified due to doping. There was no decision of the IOC redistributes the medals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dsq1_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-dsq1-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dsq3_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-dsq3-3">[3]</a></sup><br/>
<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_ee"><a href="#ref_ee"><b><sup>e</sup></b></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Iryna_Yatchenko" title="Iryna Yatchenko">Iryna Yatchenko</a> (<a href="/wiki/Belarus_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Belarus at the 2004 Summer Olympics">BLR</a>), was disqualified due to doping. The IOC decided that the bronze medal was reallocated to the athlete <a href="/wiki/V%C4%9Bra_Posp%C3%AD%C5%A1ilov%C3%A1-Cechlov%C3%A1" title="Věra Pospíšilová-Cechlová">Věra Pospíšilová-Cechlová</a> (<a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Czech Republic at the 2004 Summer Olympics">CZE</a>) during the IOC Executive Board on 30 May 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dsq1_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-dsq1-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dsq2_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-dsq2-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
